Class of 06, school was school, if you take high school with a grain of salt and just do your work and pass your classes youll do well. If you take it very sersiously and think high school is LIFE and think these are the times of my life than you're in for a HUGE let down. Theres cliques, theres sports, ASB, theatre (which was the popular all 4 years I went there) band, ect and so on. Be friends with everyone, WHO CARES. Defend those being picked on be a GOOD person and like I said before do your work and high school will be chill for you. Once a Saxon ALWAYS a Saxon, I enjoyed ALL my teachers and made a lot of friends from every group, I ate, laughed, was in musicals, sports, and ditched here and there, but I made high school right for who I am. That's all that matters.< /review>

<Time>1496010728993<//Time><Rate>5<//Rate>< Review>
Had a minimally invasive procedure , nevertheless I still needed to spend 4 days in hospital after my surgery. My first impressions lead to apprehension, but I was pleasantly surprised at the cleanliness of the hospital I arrived early at 6AM for my procedure and had a very positive experience on entering and through the check in process.

The preparation station was busy but was very professionally managed and staffed. Everyone from my immediate nurse to the anesthesiologist was very attentive and assuring. Again the station was very clean and professionally managed.

After my operation I was moved to level 6 into a private room. The 3 days I spent here were just outstanding and before I get to recognizing some of the staff that personally cared for me, I would just like to add that the rooms were ultra clean with a freshly made bed whenever possible, hospital food is just that, but when I requested a tuna on wheat sandwich I was amazed when my nurse Angus called down to the cafeteria to see if it was anywhere on the menu, disappointingly she was told no and after a short conversation with the cafeteria manager she said my sandwich would be on its way, I got the impression that the tuna would have to be brought in to the hospital. After not eating for 3 days I can tell you it was delicious, after that I was able to pick and mix food from the menu which to me was very varied in its choice for a hospital.

I had a total of 5 nurses and 6 nursing assistants. The only one negative encounter I had was with one of the nursing assistants that I can only think was not aware of my procedure and mishandled me. Other than that all of the other assistants were just great with a special thanks to Cory and Ron.

My immediate nurses were just unbelievable, professional, attentive and very understanding. In the most desperate time of my recovery I have to give a very special thanks to Ashley, she was very understanding of my requests and worked with me when I was in such pain, and at times we had a very educational discussion and she even brought a smile out of me, Ashley is a true professional a very well educated person with a great character. Another big thank you to Agnus, kamatsu, Anna and Cheryl who were all my other nurses and performed their duties attentively and again very professionally. Bianca my physical therapist was just a total dream she got me on my feet and was there at all times very professional and a great sense of humor.

I really cannot say enough about my experience at St Vincent hence my detailed review I remember commenting to Bianca that "I thought St Vincent hospital was as good as the hospitals in the UK "  where I am originally from.

Thank you St Vincent and all its staff. TC< /Review>

This place used to be a madhouse! People complain about the wait times now...you should have seen it back in the early 2000s - you don't know what a "wait time" is. Mixed feelings. Some of their stuff is truly great, but I've had a fair amount of disappointing items as well. The trick is to go for the sweet stuff ‚Äì pistachio blackberry twice-baked, chocolate claw, etc. ‚Äì because as you make your way down through the butter croissant (very good, but not amazing) towards the savory part of the menu, the quality drops dramatically.
Add to that a few other drawbacks ‚Äì long lines, early and limited hours, and a less-than-inspiring surrounding neighborhood ‚Äì and you get a bakery that has a lot of potential, but doesn't quite live up to the hype.</text>

<UserId.>103379264202553362035<//UserId.><review>Neighbor Bakehouse started as a popup in the Mr & Mrs space for about a year, eventually shutting down, much to my dismay. So, imagine my excitement when I heard they were actually getting a full brick and mortar shop!

I've been here more times than I'd like to admit since then, so, rather than boring you all with drab particulars about all their pastries, I'll just say this: everything is delicious, but they definitely excel in their savory pastries more than their sweet ones. The croissants are must-haves, and, for those with a sweet tooth, definitely grab one of the passion fruit custard filled pastries! I've seen these come in two different forms so far, but both have been delicious.

Get there before 11am and they should still have most things available. And either buy to go, or be prepared to stand around, as the limited outdoor seating does tend to be full.

***Accessibility Info***

Venue - The shop itself is just a little front area you walk in to and order from, so accessibility isn't really an issue. The seating outside is somewhat accessible: if you want to scoot in under the table, you'll have to move the benches first.

Bathroom - Didn't try them, but I'm not sure they have a public one.</review><pics>None< /pics>< rate>

1488638928635<//date>
<Rating>5</Rating>< review>
Basically the BEST bakery on earth - I don't even write Yelp reviews anymore but felt compelled as I sink my teeth into the Croque Madame I ordered this morning.  Whenever I come visit my family in the Bay Area I make a special trip out to basically order one of everything at Neighbor Bakehouse.  Been here a few times and I'm obsessed with the Croque Madame, Kimchi Toast, the Bostock and today I finally got to try the Ginger Pull Apart which was always sold out when I got there.

I'm officially a diehard Neighbor Bakehouse believer.  I mean, I would move here and move next door just so I could go here every day.  Nowadays I don't even bother going to Tartine cause everything here is so much better and consistently DELICIOUS.  The ginger pull apart is sooooo flaky and crispy and buttery it's like pastry heaven.  I mean, this place has over 300 reviews and is still a solid 5 stars.  I don't know what else I can add to this.  I don't think there's one thing here that I don't like.  They don't actually have THAT much stuff, but whenever I go I feel the need to order everything so it ends up being a lot.  Definitely get there early and make sure you're buying for a group so you can share and split stuff.  I got there at 7:30am and most everything was there - i've been there a few times at 10-11am ish and stuff would run out already. Wish there was something even 1/10th as good in NYC!< /review>

<date>1470776274763<//date><Review>Where do I begin with this place? I know - stop whatever you're doing, get in a car, √ºber, or the T line muni, arrive at Neighbor and buy the ginger pull apart. This is my favorite pastry of all time. Why? It's a myriad of textures and flavors that evoke all the best aspects of perfect baked goods. The pastry is composed of croissant dough scraps pieced together and layered with sugar and crystallized ginger. Its got a bit of that super on trend kouign Amman swagger with twice the size and twice the textural variance. The top is light and airy like those awesome bubbles that form on the crust of a pizza. Inside it's doughy and soft, like the inner layers of a cinnamon roll or raised donut. The bottom gets a crazy crystalized sugar caramelization that sticks to your teeth like ginger taffy. The aroma is buttery with dancing ginger spice and is never too sweet or too spicy. It is perfection.

And that's just one pastry!!

Neighbor doesn't get the shine of some of the hipper spots in the city but it deserves all the glory. Their croissants are perfect, and I've tried them all from plain to chocolate (claw) to everything (bagel) to salmon to blackberry pistachio. Flawless layers of fluffy flour and butter. They also have a wonderful sauerkraut tart and rotating veggie tarts that perfectly balance savory ingredients with a sweet dough. I have literally tried almost every thing this shop has to offer and have never been disappointed.

They also offer whole loaves of bread, and recently I picked up a fresh sourdough sandwich loaf ($6) and made the best French toast of my life with it. Go to neighbor. You won't regret it.

Note: normally a spot that offers little-to-no seating would get a slight dock in my book but I'm in the "pick up pastries in my PJ's and bring them home" camp rather than try to deal with the early morning dog patch fog camp.</Review>< Response>
